<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background: transparent; text-align: left; text-align:center;background-color:#efefef;">Lap leaders</div>
<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align: center; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_80be72c3906deabb5496758943c4af74"></map><img usemap="#timeline_80be72c3906deabb5496758943c4af74" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/80be72c3906deabb5496758943c4af74.png" /></div></li></ul>
</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>2002 Austrian Grand Prix</b> (formally the <b>XXVI Großer A1 Preis von Österreich</b>) was a <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> motor race held on 12 May 2002 at the <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Ring" title="Red Bull Ring">A1-Ring</a> in <a href="/wiki/Spielberg,_Styria" title="Spielberg, Styria">Spielberg, Styria</a>. It was the sixth round of the <a href="/wiki/2002_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="2002 Formula One World Championship">2002 Formula One World Championship</a> and the 25th Austrian Grand Prix as part of the Formula One World Championship. <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a> driver <a href="/wiki/Michael_Schumacher" title="Michael Schumacher">Michael Schumacher</a> won the 71-lap race after starting from third position. His teammate <a href="/wiki/Rubens_Barrichello" title="Rubens Barrichello">Rubens Barrichello</a> finished second, and <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Montoya" title="Juan Pablo Montoya">Juan Pablo Montoya</a> took third for the <a href="/wiki/Williams_Grand_Prix_Engineering" title="Williams Grand Prix Engineering">Williams</a> team.
</p><p>Barrichello started the race from the <a href="/wiki/Pole_position" title="Pole position">pole position</a> after recording the fastest lap in qualifying; Williams driver <a href="/wiki/Ralf_Schumacher" title="Ralf Schumacher">Ralf Schumacher</a> started second, but was passed by Michael Schumacher in the first corner. Barrichello maintained the lead through most of the race until Ferrari invoked <a href="/wiki/Team_orders" title="Team orders">team orders</a> on him to allow Michael Schumacher to win the race on the final lap and improve his standing in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Drivers%27_Champions" title="List of Formula One World Drivers&#39; Champions">World Drivers' Championship</a>. It was his first Austrian Grand Prix victory, his fourth in a row in the 2002 season and the 58th of his career. The <a href="/wiki/Safety_car" title="Safety car">safety car</a> was deployed twice during the race, which included a major accident on lap 28 involving <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Grand_Prix" title="Jordan Grand Prix">Jordan</a> driver <a href="/wiki/Takuma_Sato" title="Takuma Sato">Takuma Sato</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nick_Heidfeld" title="Nick Heidfeld">Nick Heidfeld</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sauber_Motorsport" title="Sauber Motorsport">Sauber</a> team, who both sustained light injuries.
</p><p>At the post-race podium ceremony Michael Schumacher implored Barrichello to mount the stand reserved for the race winner and gave the first-place trophy to his teammate. That led the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="Fédération Internationale de l&#39;Automobile">Fédération Internationale de l'Automobile</a> (FIA; Formula One's governing body) to fine Ferrari, Michael Schumacher and Barrichello $1 million on 26 June; each paid a third immediately, while the remainder was suspended. Following a review, the FIA banned the practice of team orders beginning with the <a href="/wiki/2003_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="2003 Formula One World Championship">2003 season</a>; they began again allowing the practice following the <a href="/wiki/2010_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="2010 Formula One World Championship">2010 championship</a>.
</p><p>The win increased Michael Schumacher's lead in the World Drivers' Championship to 27 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Championship_points_scoring_systems" title="List of Formula One World Championship points scoring systems">points</a> over Montoya in second place. Ralf Schumacher came fourth to maintain third place, and Barrichello moved past <a href="/wiki/David_Coulthard" title="David Coulthard">David Coulthard</a> of the <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a> team to fourth. In the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Constructors%27_Champions" title="List of Formula One World Constructors&#39; Champions">World Constructors' Championship</a>, Ferrari further extended their advantage over Williams to 16 points. McLaren were another 36 points behind in third with eleven races remaining in the season.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2002_Austrian_Grand_Prix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Red_Bull_Ring,_April_18,_2018_SkySat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Aerial photograph of the AI Ring, now called the Red Bull Ring, where the race was held" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Red_Bull_Ring%2C_April_18%2C_2018_SkySat.jpg/220px-Red_Bull_Ring%2C_April_18%2C_2018_SkySat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Red_Bull_Ring%2C_April_18%2C_2018_SkySat.jpg/330px-Red_Bull_Ring%2C_April_18%2C_2018_SkySat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Red_Bull_Ring%2C_April_18%2C_2018_SkySat.jpg/440px-Red_Bull_Ring%2C_April_18%2C_2018_SkySat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2023" data-file-height="1518" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Red_Bull_Ring,_April_18,_2018_SkySat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Ring" title="Red Bull Ring">A1 Ring</a>, now called the Red Bull Ring <i>(pictured in 2018)</i>, where the race was held.</div></div></div>
<p>The 2002 <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Grand_Prix" title="Austrian Grand Prix">Austrian Grand Prix</a> was the 6th of 17 motor races in the <a href="/wiki/2002_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="2002 Formula One World Championship">2002 Formula One World Championship</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CF1Overview_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CF1Overview-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and the 25th time it formed part of the championship.<sup id="cite_ref-CrashPreview_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashPreview-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The 71-lap race was held at the 9-turn 4.326&#160;km (2.688&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Ring" title="Red Bull Ring">A1 Ring</a> in <a href="/wiki/Spielberg,_Styria" title="Spielberg, Styria">Spielberg, Styria</a>, on 12 May.<sup id="cite_ref-CF1Overview_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CF1Overview-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CrashPreview_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashPreview-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> With very few sections requiring drivers competitors to slow down, the track gives teams an opportunity to push their engines to their full potential. 70 percent of the lap can be driven at full racing speed, although the circuit's relatively high altitude of 700&#160;m (2,300&#160;ft) offers less oxygen to feed the combustion engines, reducing their performance by approximately seven percent.<sup id="cite_ref-CrashPreview_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashPreview-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Having won four of the season's five previous races, <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a> driver <a href="/wiki/Michael_Schumacher" title="Michael Schumacher">Michael Schumacher</a> led the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Drivers%27_Champions" title="List of Formula One World Drivers&#39; Champions">Drivers' Championship</a> with 44 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Championship_points_scoring_systems" title="List of Formula One World Championship points scoring systems">points</a>. <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Montoya" title="Juan Pablo Montoya">Juan Pablo Montoya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ralf_Schumacher" title="Ralf Schumacher">Ralf Schumacher</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Williams_Grand_Prix_Engineering" title="Williams Grand Prix Engineering">Williams</a> team were second and third with 23 and 20 points, respectively. Driving for <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Coulthard" title="David Coulthard">David Coulthard</a> was fourth with nine points, and <a href="/wiki/Jenson_Button" title="Jenson Button">Jenson Button</a> for <a href="/wiki/Renault_in_Formula_One" title="Renault in Formula One">Renault</a> was a further point behind in fifth.<sup id="cite_ref-2002points_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2002points-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Ferrari led the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Constructors%27_Champions" title="List of Formula One World Constructors&#39; Champions">Constructors' Championship</a>with 50 points, seven ahead of Williams in second place. McLaren with 13 points were third, with Renault and <a href="/wiki/Sauber_Motorsport" title="Sauber Motorsport">Sauber</a> tied for fourth with eight points apiece.<sup id="cite_ref-2002points_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2002points-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Michael Schumacher was strongly considered by the British press,<sup id="cite_ref-STPreview_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STPreview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> bookmakers,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and former drivers <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Berger" title="Gerhard Berger">Gerhard Berger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niki_Lauda" title="Niki Lauda">Niki Lauda</a> the favourite to win the Austrian Grand Prix, an event he had not won in four previous attempts.<sup id="cite_ref-STPreview_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STPreview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He said of his chances in Austria, "We believe we have a very competitive package overall but it's a question of how good the others can be".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He expressed confidence he could challenge for victory saying, "I certainly won't be approaching this race any differently than the others. And with two almost perfect races behind us, I'm obviously looking forward to the Austrian Grand Prix with a lot of confidence."<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Montoya stated he would be better able to challenge Ferrari at the A1-Ring recalling the team's strong form in 2001 despite scoring no points, "I am pretty confident that in Austria we will be quite strong, certainly stronger than in [the prior race in] <a href="/wiki/2002_Spanish_Grand_Prix" title="2002 Spanish Grand Prix">Barcelona</a>, so I am looking forward to it."<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In technical developments, Sauber introduced a revised evolution of its Ferrari 050 engine that the team had used in the first five races of the 2002 championship. The team installed a new aerodynamic package that included a revised undertray, front wing and altered bodywork around the cover of the <a href="/wiki/Sauber_C21" title="Sauber C21">C21</a>'s engine. The Ferrari, McLaren and Williams teams brought new front brake <a href="/wiki/Intake" title="Intake">air intakes</a>. Williams also used an upgraded front wing on its <a href="/wiki/Williams_FW24" title="Williams FW24">FW24</a>, which was characterised by a curved profile <sup id="cite_ref-Piola_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Piola-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Practice">Practice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2002_Austrian_Grand_Prix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Practice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Four practice sessions were held before the Sunday race, two each on Friday and Saturday. The Friday morning and afternoon sessions each lasted an hour; the third and fourth sessions, on Saturday morning, lasted 45 minutes each.<sup id="cite_ref-regulations_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The first practice session was held in cool and overcast weather. Michael Schumacher was fastest with a lap of 1 minute, 11.072 seconds with approximately ten minutes remaining. His teammate Barrichello, <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Massa" title="Felipe Massa">Felipe Massa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nick_Heidfeld" title="Nick Heidfeld">Nick Heidfeld</a> of Sauber, <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Grand_Prix" title="Jordan Grand Prix">Jordan</a> drivers <a href="/wiki/Giancarlo_Fisichella" title="Giancarlo Fisichella">Giancarlo Fisichella</a> and <a href="/wiki/Takuma_Sato" title="Takuma Sato">Takuma Sato</a>, Coulthard, <a href="/wiki/Arrows_Grand_Prix_International" title="Arrows Grand Prix International">Arrows</a>' <a href="/wiki/Heinz-Harald_Frentzen" title="Heinz-Harald Frentzen">Heinz-Harald Frentzen</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/British_American_Racing" title="British American Racing">British American Racing</a> (BAR) duo of <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Villeneuve" title="Jacques Villeneuve">Jacques Villeneuve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Olivier_Panis" title="Olivier Panis">Olivier Panis</a>, were second through tenth.<sup id="cite_ref-AF1FP1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AF1FP1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Some drivers—including Barrichello, Massa and Fisichella—ran off the dusty, slippery track into a <a href="/wiki/Run-off_area" title="Run-off area">gravel trap</a> during the session because of a low amount of <a href="/wiki/Grip_(auto_racing)" title="Grip (auto racing)">grip</a>; none sustained damage to their vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-AF1FP1_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AF1FP1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FIAFriday_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIAFriday-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Conditions became warmer and sunnier for the second practice session though rainfall threatened towards the end.<sup id="cite_ref-F1NetFP1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1NetFP1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The fastest times to be recorded within the first 20 minutes since the track temperature was at its warmest.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Barrichello set the day's fastest lap, at 1 minute, 10.549 seconds. His teammate Michael Schumacher was three-hundredths of a second slower in second position. Montoya, <a href="/wiki/Kimi_R%C3%A4ikk%C3%B6nen" title="Kimi Räikkönen">Kimi Räikkönen</a> of the McLaren team, <a href="/wiki/Allan_McNish" title="Allan McNish">Allan McNish</a> for <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Racing_(Formula_One_team)" title="Toyota Racing (Formula One team)">Toyota</a>, Arrows driver <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Bernoldi" title="Enrique Bernoldi">Enrique Bernoldi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Racing" title="Jaguar Racing">Jaguar</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_la_Rosa" title="Pedro de la Rosa">Pedro de la Rosa</a>, Panis, Coulthard and Sato were third to tenth.<sup id="cite_ref-AF1FP2_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AF1FP2-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Some drivers, including Michael and Ralf Schumacher, and McNish, again lost control of their cars and ran off to the side of the track during the session.<sup id="cite_ref-F1NetFP1_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1NetFP1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AF1FP2_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AF1FP2-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Heidfeld's track time was curtailed after 20 minutes due to an <a href="/wiki/Alternator_(automotive)" title="Alternator (automotive)">alternator</a> fault.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Frentzen lost a quarter of an hour to familiarise himself with the track after he spun over a <a href="/wiki/Curb" title="Curb">kerb</a> and damaged his car's undertray.<sup id="cite_ref-FIAFriday_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIAFriday-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The third practice session took place in clear and dry weather; no drivers ventured off the less slippery circuit.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Michael Schumacher used low track and ambient temperatures to become the first driver to go below 70 seconds all weekend with a lap of 1 minute, 9.001 seconds that he recorded half an hour in.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DF1FP3_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1FP3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> His teammate Barrichello was second-fastest and Räikkönen third. Frentzen, Massa, Coulthard, Heidfeld, Panis, Button and Bernoldi followed in positions four through ten.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1FP3_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1FP3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The ambient and track temperatures had increased by the start of the fourth practice session.<sup id="cite_ref-F1NetFP4_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1NetFP4-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Several competitors made driver errors that sent them into a gravel trap.<sup id="cite_ref-AutosportFP4_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutosportFP4-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Michael Schumacher set the track record, with a lap of 1 minute, 8.433 seconds. Barrichello was second, and Ralf Schumacher improved to third. Montoya, Frentzen, Massa, Heidfeld, Räikkönen, Panis and Villeneuve completed the top ten.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Bernoldi missed 25 minutes due to a malfunctioning gearbox. He later lost control of the rear of his car at turn two and beached in a gravel trap before the session ended.<sup id="cite_ref-F1NetFP4_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1NetFP4-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutosportFP4_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutosportFP4-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Qualifying">Qualifying</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2002_Austrian_Grand_Prix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Qualifying">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barrichello_2002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of Rubens Barrichello in a red racing suit" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Barrichello_2002.jpg/170px-Barrichello_2002.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Barrichello_2002.jpg/255px-Barrichello_2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Barrichello_2002.jpg/340px-Barrichello_2002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1128" data-file-height="1975" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barrichello_2002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rubens_Barrichello" title="Rubens Barrichello">Rubens Barrichello</a> took his second <a href="/wiki/Pole_position" title="Pole position">pole position</a> of the 2002 season and the fifth of his career</div></div></div>
<p>Saturday's afternoon one-hour qualifying session saw each competitor limited to twelve laps, with the starting order decided by their fastest laps. The <a href="/wiki/107%25_rule" title="107% rule">107% rule</a> was in effect during this session, requiring each driver set a time within 107 per cent of the quickest lap to qualify for the race.<sup id="cite_ref-regulations_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Conditions were clear with warm air and track temperatures.<sup id="cite_ref-FIASaturday_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIASaturday-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DTQuali_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTQuali-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Barrichello took his second <a href="/wiki/Pole_position" title="Pole position">pole position</a> of the season and the fifth of his career with a lap of 1 minute, 8.082 seconds.<sup id="cite_ref-UPIPole_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPIPole-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> He was joined on the <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_motorsport_terms#G" title="Glossary of motorsport terms">grid</a>'s front row by Ralf Schumacher, who took his best starting position of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-UPIPole_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPIPole-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Michael Schumacher was third; he said he lost speed due to a brake problem, and traffic baulked him.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Quotes_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Quotes-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> He switched to the spare Ferrari for his final timed lap in an unsuccessful attempt to claim pole position,<sup id="cite_ref-AutosportQuali_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutosportQuali-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DTQuali_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTQuali-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and did not earn a front-row start for the first time since the <a href="/wiki/2001_Italian_Grand_Prix" title="2001 Italian Grand Prix">2001 Italian Grand Prix</a> eight races earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-ObserverQuali_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ObserverQuali-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> A misfiring engine prompted Montoya in fourth to switch to the spare car <a href="/wiki/Racing_setup" title="Racing setup">setup</a> for his teammate Ralf Schumacher; he made a minor tyre-pressure adjustment to record his fastest lap.<sup id="cite_ref-FIASaturday_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIASaturday-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Heidfeld took fifth, claiming he could have improved had Button not slowed his final timed lap. A lack of speed restricted the McLaren duo of Räikkönen and Coulthard to sixth and eighth; they were separated by Massa who made two driver errors in an unbalanced car through high-speed turns. Panis set the ninth-fastest time as de la Rosa slowed his final timed lap. Toyota's <a href="/wiki/Mika_Salo" title="Mika Salo">Mika Salo</a> in tenth had a minor <a href="/wiki/Understeer_and_oversteer" title="Understeer and oversteer">understeer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Quotes_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Quotes-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Frentzen in 11th spun on oil and removed some bodywork components from his car in a gravel trap. His vehicle was later repaired to continue driving.<sup id="cite_ref-FIASaturday_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIASaturday-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutosportQuali_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutosportQuali-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> His Arrows' teammate Bernoldi followed in 12th and expressed satisfaction with his car's balance.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Quotes_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Quotes-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Traffic slowed Button on his four timed laps and left him 13th.<sup id="cite_ref-SundayTimesQuali_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SundayTimesQuali-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> McNish and Toyota located a car setup tailored to suit him, and took 14th.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Quotes_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Quotes-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Fisichella ran a new engine in qualifying and took 15th with a car setup suited for used front and new rear tyres.<sup id="cite_ref-FIASaturday_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIASaturday-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jarno_Trulli" title="Jarno Trulli">Jarno Trulli</a> had a major engine failure through turn nine and lost control of his Renault on the leaked oil from the engine failure.<sup id="cite_ref-AutosportQuali_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutosportQuali-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The session was stopped for 11 minutes for <a href="/wiki/Motorsport_marshal" title="Motorsport marshal">track marshals</a> to dry it.<sup id="cite_ref-ObserverQuali_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ObserverQuali-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Trulli returned to his garage and used the spare Renault setup for his teammate Button and took 16th after minor braking problems. Villeneuve used a new set of tyres for qualifying; he was uncomfortable with his car's setup and was 17th. A handling imbalance created an unbalanced car for Sato in 18th. Jaguar's de la Rosa and <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Irvine" title="Eddie Irvine">Eddie Irvine</a> filled the grid's tenth row: de la Rosa had a rear suspension fault caused by an <a href="/wiki/Exhaust_system" title="Exhaust system">exhaust</a> overheating it and Irvine removed his front wing in a collision with the rear of Bernoldi's vehicle into turn one. <a href="/wiki/Minardi" title="Minardi">Minardi</a> drivers <a href="/wiki/Mark_Webber" title="Mark Webber">Mark Webber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Yoong" title="Alex Yoong">Alex Yoong</a> started from the eleventh row: Webber optimised his <a href="/wiki/Minardi_PS02" title="Minardi PS02">PS02</a>'s balance so it ran without any issues on its tyres during the session, and intermittent rear brake locking destabilised Yoong's car causing him to spin after he exited the pit lane.<sup id="cite_ref-FIASaturday_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIASaturday-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DF1Quotes_28-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Quotes-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Warm-up">Warm-up</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2002_Austrian_Grand_Prix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Warm-up">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A half hour warm-up session took place on Sunday morning,<sup id="cite_ref-regulations_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> in clear and warm weather conditions. All drivers fine-tuned their race setups for the weather and drove their spare cars.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Barrichello had the fastest lap of 1 minute and 10.876 seconds and his teammate Michael Schumacher was second. Massa, Frentzen, Heidfeld, Bernoldi, Coulthard, Villeneuve, Räikkönen and Irvine completed the top ten.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> While the session saw no major incidents, Ralf Schumacher entered the gravel traps at the two of the track's corners.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the warm-up session, Montoya predicted several drivers would run wide on a <a href="/wiki/Rumble_strip" title="Rumble strip">rumble strip</a> located to the outside of the circuit, which extended from turn one to the first portion of the <a href="/wiki/Straight_(racing)" title="Straight (racing)">straight</a> driving towards turn two, to increase the top speed of their cars.<sup id="cite_ref-WhitingSatMeeting_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhitingSatMeeting-37">&#91;N 1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MontoyaPreRace_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MontoyaPreRace-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ron_Dennis" title="Ron Dennis">Ron Dennis</a>, the team principal of McLaren, argued Ferrari should allow their drivers to race each other without the imposition of <a href="/wiki/Team_orders" title="Team orders">team orders</a> favouring one driver over the other as had happened in the <a href="/wiki/2001_Austrian_Grand_Prix" title="2001 Austrian Grand Prix">2001 race</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Race">Race</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2002_Austrian_Grand_Prix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Race">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The race began at 14:00 local time;<sup id="cite_ref-CF1Overview_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CF1Overview-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> the weather was clear and dry. The air temperature was 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F) and the track temperature ranged from 27 to 29&#160;°C (81 to 84&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-F1NetRace_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1NetRace-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-F1COMRace_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1COMRace-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Barrichello made a brisk start to maintain the lead into the first turn.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCWebRace_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCWebRace-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> While he provided room for drivers to pass him, none did.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Behind Barrichello, his teammate Michael Schumacher made a fast start to slot into second position and Heidfeld rose from fifth to third having overtaken Ralf Schumacher on the outside.<sup id="cite_ref-F1NetRace_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1NetRace-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Räikkönen and Massa, meanwhile, drew alongside and Massa steered onto the grass<sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> dropping to tenth. Further back, Bernoldi made contact with the rear of his teammate Frentzen;<sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> both cars continued as Bernoldi entered the pit lane after the first lap.<sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> At turn two, an increase in speed led de la Rosa's <a href="/wiki/Throttle" title="Throttle">throttle</a> pick-up to start to cut out.<sup id="cite_ref-F1COMRace_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1COMRace-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> He slowed, and retired in the pit lane at the end of the lap. In the meantime, Villeneuve experienced a minor loss of car control and hit Frentzen's car on the inside.<sup id="cite_ref-CrashRace_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashRace-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The collision sent Frentzen into a gravel trap from which he slowly extricated himself.<sup id="cite_ref-F1NetRace_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1NetRace-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CrashRace_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashRace-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Juan_Pablo_Montoya_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of Juan Pablo Montoya dressed in white looking to his left" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Juan_Pablo_Montoya_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Juan_Pablo_Montoya_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/Juan_Pablo_Montoya_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="198" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Juan_Pablo_Montoya_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Montoya" title="Juan Pablo Montoya">Juan Pablo Montoya</a> <i>(pictured at the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Grand_Prix" title="United States Grand Prix">United States Grand Prix</a> later in 2002)</i> finished in third position</div></div></div>
<p>At the end of the first lap, Barrichello led his teammate Michael Schumacher, Heidfeld, Ralf Schumacher, Montoya and Coulthard.<sup id="cite_ref-F1COMRace_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1COMRace-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Heidfeld ran wide at Castrol Kurve at the beginning of the second lap and the Williams pair of Ralf Schumacher and Montoya demoted him to fifth.<sup id="cite_ref-CrashRace_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashRace-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Barrichello and Michael Schumacher began to pull away from the rest of the field.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCWebRace_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCWebRace-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> There were overtakes further down the field. On lap two, Salo passed Button for eighth position.<sup id="cite_ref-F1COMRace_40-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1COMRace-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Villeneuve overtook his teammate Panis for 14th position and Frentzen passed Webber on lap three.<sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> During the next lap Yoong lost two places to his teammate Webber, and Frentzen.<sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Bernoldi retired from the race with a broken front wing and front brake pipe.<sup id="cite_ref-F1COMRace_40-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1COMRace-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Räikkönen in seventh retired at the side of the track with an engine failure on lap six.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MCOMRace_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCOMRace-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On lap seven Villeneuve passed McNish for tenth place, then ran wide. He made a second, successful attempt on the eighth lap, passing McNish who opted against a challenge.<sup id="cite_ref-F1COMRace_40-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1COMRace-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>That same lap, Massa entered the pit lane to join the list of retirees with a failed left-rear <a href="/wiki/Car_suspension" title="Car suspension">suspension</a> bracket; it failed in turn two, causing the Sauber C21's right-front wheel to lift from the tarmac surface and its undertray to scrape along it. Villeneuve made a pass on Fisichella for ninth place on lap ten.<sup id="cite_ref-F1COMRace_40-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1COMRace-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Not long after Villeneuve overtook Button for eighth position. By the same lap, Barrichello led by a second over his teammate Michael Schumacher, who in turn was 17 seconds ahead of Ralf Schumacher. Further down the order, Frentzen put a rear wheel on the grass at the final corner on lap 16. He lost control of his car, spun through 180 degrees and rolled backwards in front of the race leaders. Frentzen fell to 18th position, behind the Minardi cars of Webber and Yoong. He passed Yoong to return to 17th position on the 18th lap.<sup id="cite_ref-F1NetRace_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1NetRace-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-F1COMRace_40-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1COMRace-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> One lap later, Villeneuve overtook Salo on the inside for seventh place and blocked his attempted counter-move.<sup id="cite_ref-F1COMRace_40-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1COMRace-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCWebRace_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCWebRace-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As the Ferraris extended their lead over Ralf Schumacher, the stewards informed the BAR team on the 23rd lap that Villeneuve had incurred a <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_regulations#Penalties" title="Formula One regulations">drive-through penalty</a> as they deemed him at fault for the collision with Frentzen on lap one.<sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Lap 24 saw the <a href="/wiki/Safety_car" title="Safety car">safety car</a>'s first deployment: Panis' engine failed without warning on the start/finish straight.<sup id="cite_ref-CrashRace_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashRace-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> His rear wheels locked, spun to the centre of the track and avoided colliding with a barrier.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GPCOMRace_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPCOMRace-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Track marshals removed Panis' car from the circuit as he returned to the pit lane.<sup id="cite_ref-IHTRace_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHTRace-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The Ferrari and Williams' teams employed different pit stop strategies—the Ferrari team planned for  two stops whereas the Williams team planned one.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MCOMRace_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCOMRace-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The Ferrari team called Barrichello and Michael Schumacher into the pit lane for their first <a href="/wiki/Pit_stop" title="Pit stop">pit stops</a>; Schumacher drove more slowly than Barrichello to allow their mechanics to service the latter's car first. Barrichello retained the lead as Michael Schumacher yielded second to Ralf Schumacher. The safety car was withdrawn at the conclusion of the 27th lap and Barrichello led at the restart.<sup id="cite_ref-F1NetRace_39-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1NetRace-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Takuma_Sato.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of Takuma Saot seated behind a table with a pen in hand" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Takuma_Sato.jpg/170px-Takuma_Sato.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Takuma_Sato.jpg/255px-Takuma_Sato.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Takuma_Sato.jpg/340px-Takuma_Sato.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1704" data-file-height="2272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Takuma_Sato.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Takuma_Sato" title="Takuma Sato">Takuma Sato</a> <i>(pictured in 2002)</i> was involved in a heavy accident that caused soft-tissue damage to his right thigh</div></div></div>
<p>Soon after, a major accident prompted the safety car's second deployment on lap 28.<sup id="cite_ref-SpeedRace_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpeedRace-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> As the field entered turn two,<sup id="cite_ref-IHTRace_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHTRace-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Heidfeld noticed smoke coming from Yoong's Minardi and applied his cold brakes heavily. This locked the Sauber's rear wheels and sent him out of control about 100&#160;yd (91&#160;m) from the <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_motorsport_terms#A" title="Glossary of motorsport terms">apex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CrashRace_45-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashRace-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> He veered into the grass as his car spun 180 degrees;<sup id="cite_ref-IHTRace_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHTRace-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SpeedRace_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpeedRace-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> the grass did not slow him,<sup id="cite_ref-CrashRace_45-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashRace-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and he was launched over the crest of a hill.<sup id="cite_ref-SpeedRace_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpeedRace-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Montoya on the inside was about to lap Sato's slower car at turn two, with the latter ahead of him at the turn's apex.<sup id="cite_ref-SatoCrash_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SatoCrash-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> At high speed,<sup id="cite_ref-SatoCrash_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SatoCrash-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Heidfeld narrowly avoided a collision with Montoya's front wing,<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> and the rear of his Sauber sustained a <a href="/wiki/Side_collision" title="Side collision">side collision</a> against the right-hand sidepod of Sato's car,<sup id="cite_ref-F1NetRace_39-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1NetRace-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DawnRace_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DawnRace-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> causing heavy damage to both vehicles and littering carbon fibre and titanium debris on a wide area of track.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Heidfeld's rear structure and titanium gearbox punctured a hole in Sato's car; his knees struck the steering column breaking it in half.<sup id="cite_ref-SatoExtraction_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SatoExtraction-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Both drivers were sent into a gravel trap and came to a stop there.<sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A visibly shaken Heidfeld was extricated from his car by track marshals with a heavily bruised left leg.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MCOMRace_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCOMRace-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Sato remained in his car with soft-tissue damage to his right thigh<sup id="cite_ref-IHTRace_47-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHTRace-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> but did not lose consciousness;<sup id="cite_ref-SatoExtraction_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SatoExtraction-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> a section of the Sauber's rear crash structure penetrated the side of the Jordan's monocoque just below Sato's right knee and his <a href="/wiki/Racing_helmet" title="Racing helmet">helmet</a> was squeezed between the car's <a href="/wiki/Head_restraint" title="Head restraint">head restraint</a>, both of which prevented him from leaving his car.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SatoExtraction_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SatoExtraction-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="Fédération Internationale de l&#39;Automobile">Fédération Internationale de l'Automobile</a> (FIA, Formula One's governing body) safety and medical delegate <a href="/wiki/Sid_Watkins" title="Sid Watkins">Sid Watkins</a> and his team took ten minutes to remove Sato from the car and treated him at the crash site before transporting him by ambulance to the track's medical centre.<sup id="cite_ref-MCOMRace_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCOMRace-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IHTRace_47-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHTRace-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> From there,<sup id="cite_ref-GPCOMRace_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPCOMRace-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Sato and Heidfeld were flown by helicopter to <a href="/wiki/Medical_University_of_Graz" title="Medical University of Graz">Graz University Hospital</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-IHTRace_47-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHTRace-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MCOMRace_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCOMRace-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> for overnight observation and precautionary x-ray scans.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Under safety car conditions, every team except for Ferrari and Williams brought their drivers to the pit lane for additional fuel and a set of tyres.<sup id="cite_ref-CrashRace_45-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashRace-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> After 20 minutes,<sup id="cite_ref-IHTRace_47-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHTRace-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> the race restarted at the end of the 36th lap when the safety car entered the pit lane. Barrichello led Ralf Schumacher, Michael Schumacher, Montoya, Coulthard and Fisichella. On lap 37, Webber passed his teammate Yoong for 13th position.<sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Villeneuve passed Fisichella for sixth place at the start of the 38th lap.<sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> On the same lap, Irvine entered the pit lane to retire with a hydraulics failure.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Two laps later, Villeneuve caught and overtook Coulthard at turn one for fifth position.<sup id="cite_ref-F1COMRace_40-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1COMRace-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Coulthard lost sixth place to Fisichella after he drove on oil and off the circuit on the 45th lap.<sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> On the same lap Trulli pulled over at the end of the pit lane wall on the main straight to retire from with a loss of <a href="/wiki/Pressure_regulator" title="Pressure regulator">fuel pressure</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-F1COMRace_40-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1COMRace-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Yoong retired with fire visible from the rear of his Minardi not long after.<sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Green flag pit stops began on lap 47. Ralf Schumacher made a pit stop and dropped to fifth position. His teammate Montoya remained on the track for another four laps and used more fuel in an attempt to overtake Ralf Schumacher.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Montoya entered the pit lane for tyres on the 51st lap.<sup id="cite_ref-CrashRace_45-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashRace-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> He returned to the race in fourth position, ahead of his teammate Ralf Schumacher.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Villeneuve was elevated to third position until a pit stop on lap 53 demoted him to ninth. Montoya and Ralf Schumacher returned to third and fourth respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-FIARace_43-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIARace-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2002_Austrian_GP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph showing Rubens Barrichello making way to allow Michael Schumacher to cross the finish line ahead of him" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/2002_Austrian_GP.jpg/220px-2002_Austrian_GP.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/2002_Austrian_GP.jpg/330px-2002_Austrian_GP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/2002_Austrian_GP.jpg/440px-2002_Austrian_GP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="698" data-file-height="514" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2002_Austrian_GP.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ferrari invoked <a href="/wiki/Team_orders" title="Team orders">team orders</a> to allow <a href="/wiki/Michael_Schumacher" title="Michael Schumacher">Michael Schumacher</a> past his teammate Rubens Barrichello to win the race and earn the maximum number of points towards the World Drivers' Championship.</div></div></div>
<p>Barrichello entered the pit lane for the second time on the 61st lap. His fuel stop took 6.2 seconds and he exited in second place. His teammate Michael Schumacher led lap 62 and made his second pit stop at the end of the lap. He returned to the race in second position; Barrichello returned to first.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCWebRace_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCWebRace-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On the 63rd lap,<sup id="cite_ref-GPCOMRace_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPCOMRace-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Ferrari team principal <a href="/wiki/Jean_Todt" title="Jean Todt">Jean Todt</a> invoked team orders on Barrichello to relinquish the victory to his teammate Michael Schumacher.<sup id="cite_ref-LaStampaTodt_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaStampaTodt-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TeamOrders_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TeamOrders-53">&#91;N 2&#93;</a></sup> This would improve Schumacher's position in the World Drivers' Championship with a win earning him ten points. Ferrari advised Barrichello they would terminate his contract if he failed to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-TerraBAR_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TerraBAR-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Barrichello reminded Todt over the radio of a promise he made not to relinquish a victory to a driver. This prompted Todt to reply to Barrichello that he was required to obey his instruction to preserve Ferrari's "best interests".<sup id="cite_ref-TODisobey_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TODisobey-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Personnel on the Ferrari pit gantry observed the television screens and noticed Michael Schumacher could not get close enough to pass Barrichello in the final seven laps.<sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the start of the final lap, Barrichello led his teammate Michael Schumacher by one second.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCWebRace_41-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCWebRace-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> As Barrichello entered the final corner,<sup id="cite_ref-BBCWebRace_41-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCWebRace-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Ferrari technical director <a href="/wiki/Ross_Brawn" title="Ross Brawn">Ross Brawn</a> informed Michael Schumacher over the radio his teammate would yield to him.<sup id="cite_ref-CrashRace_45-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrashRace-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> When Barrichello braked in the final 100 to 50&#160;yd (91 to 46&#160;m),<sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SpeedRace_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpeedRace-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Michael Schumacher slowed more than his teammate because he had hoped that no team orders would be applied as Barrichello did the same to comply with Ferrari's instruction.<sup id="cite_ref-IERace_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IERace-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Schumacher passed Barrichello for his first victory in Austria, his fourth in a row in 2002, and the 58th of his career in a time of 1 hour, 33 minutes and 51.562 seconds at an average speed of 196.334&#160;km/h (121.996&#160;mph).<sup id="cite_ref-DawnRace_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DawnRace-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Barrichello was 0.182 seconds behind in second position with Montoya 17.7 seconds adrift in third. Montoya's teammate Ralf Schumacher finished in fourth place.<sup id="cite_ref-SpeedRace_48-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpeedRace-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Fisichella was fifth and took the first two points of the season for the Jordan team. Coulthard took the final point in sixth position, ahead of Button's Renault and the Toyota cars of Salo and McNish.<sup id="cite_ref-MCOMRace_46-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCOMRace-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> A loss of hydraulic pressure caused Villeneuve's engine to fail on the final lap; he was classified tenth.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Frentzen and Webber for the Arrows and Minardi teams were the final finishers, albeit two laps behind the race winner.<sup id="cite_ref-DawnRace_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DawnRace-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-race">Post-race</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2002_Austrian_Grand_Prix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Post-race">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Ferrari team were booed, jeered, whistled at and given a thumbs down signal by the crowd in <i><a href="/wiki/Parc_ferm%C3%A9" title="Parc fermé">parc fermé</a></i> and on the podium.<sup id="cite_ref-MCOMRace_46-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCOMRace-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IHTRace_47-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHTRace-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Michael Schumacher insisted Barrichello to mount the first position on the podium, as "<a href="/wiki/Deutschlandlied" title="Deutschlandlied">Deutschlandlied</a>" was played.<sup id="cite_ref-GPCOMRace_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPCOMRace-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Schumacher then stood next to his teammate during the composition of <a href="/wiki/Il_Canto_degli_Italiani" title="Il Canto degli Italiani">Il Canto degli Italiani</a> <sup id="cite_ref-DF1Review_42-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF1Review-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Sch%C3%BCssel" title="Wolfgang Schüssel">Wolfgang Schüssel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Austria" title="Chancellor of Austria">Chancellor of Austria</a>, presented the winner's trophy to Schumacher, the latter gave it to Barrichello.<sup id="cite_ref-IHTRace_47-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHTRace-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Later, in the press conference, where loud boos were heard,<sup id="cite_ref-IHTRace_47-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHTRace-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Barrichello said of the situation, "I'm going through a period of a very good time of my life. I'm becoming a better person, a better driver, so there's no point in arguing. I think my determination will bring me a lot more wins, so that's the way I see it, so there's no point arguing."<sup id="cite_ref-PressConf_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PressConf-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Michael Schumacher said he understood Ferrari's decision, "the team is investing a lot of money for one sort of target and imagine in the end it wouldn't be enough by this amount of points, how stupid would we look?"<sup id="cite_ref-PressConf_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PressConf-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Montoya said the two safety car periods allowed him to pass his teammate Ralf Schumacher, "Ralf was quite quick out of the pits as well, but I managed to get a few laps in really quick right before the stop and that was enough."<sup id="cite_ref-PressConf_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PressConf-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sato and Heidfeld were deemed fit to compete at the next race of the season, the <a href="/wiki/2002_Monaco_Grand_Prix" title="2002 Monaco Grand Prix">Monaco Grand Prix</a> two weeks later, after they passed fitness tests.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Sid Watkins told <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Jordan" title="Eddie Jordan">Eddie Jordan</a>, the owner of the Jordan team, that Sato had "a miraculous escape", leading Jordan to remark, "Somebody up there likes him".<sup id="cite_ref-DawnRace_50-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DawnRace-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Sato said he had not observed Heidfeld approaching him, "When I opened my eyes I could see my legs were squashed by the damaged monocoque and I could see the ground through the hole. Although there was some pain, I knew nothing was broken. The car did a great job of saving me – I hear there was nothing left of it."<sup id="cite_ref-SatoCrash_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SatoCrash-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Heidfeld admitted he was at fault for causing the crash, "I saw a cloud of tyre smoke as [Alex] Yoong braked really hard and early ahead of us, and maybe I pressed the pedal too hard as a result while the brakes were still cool. The car got away from me and next thing I knew I was going backwards down the grass."<sup id="cite_ref-SatoCrash_49-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SatoCrash-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> That the injuries Sato sustained in the accident were minor was cited as a consequence of improved safety standards undertaken by the FIA, racing teams and medical experts since the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-SatoExtraction_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SatoExtraction-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ralf Schumacher praised his car for allowing him to finish fourth, "Due to the action packed race and the different strategies it is difficult to say how big Ferrari's advantage really was here on the A1-Ring. We have to continue to work hard, this much is clear."<sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Fisichella commented on his fifth-place finish, "It's been a very, very good day for me, as I didn't expect to score points. But, the most important thing is that Takuma is alright. It felt fantastic when I crossed the line and I would like to say thank you to the team, especially because we made the right pit stop decision."<sup id="cite_ref-Auto1Race_44-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto1Race-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The race result increased Michael Schumacher's lead in the Drivers' Championship to 27 points over Montoya in second place. Ralf Schumacher was third with 23 points. Barrichello moved past Coulthard for fourth with 12 points.<sup id="cite_ref-2002points_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2002points-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In the Constructors' Championship, Ferrari further extended their advantage over the Williams team to 16 points. McLaren maintained third position with 14 points. The Renault and Sauber teams continued to hold fourth and fifth places with eleven races left in the season.<sup id="cite_ref-2002points_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2002points-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_orders">Team orders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2002_Austrian_Grand_Prix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Team orders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Ferrari team's use of team orders to determine the finishing order overshadowed the race.<sup id="cite_ref-IHTRace_47-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHTRace-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DawnRace_50-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DawnRace-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a></i> cited it as the most "particularly blatant" application of team orders applied to favour one driver over another since Coulthard relinquished first position to his McLaren teammate <a href="/wiki/Mika_H%C3%A4kkinen" title="Mika Häkkinen">Mika Häkkinen</a> in the final laps of the <a href="/wiki/1998_Australian_Grand_Prix" title="1998 Australian Grand Prix">1998 Australian Grand Prix</a> to comply with a prior agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Australian commentator <a href="/wiki/Darrell_Eastlake" title="Darrell Eastlake">Darrell Eastlake</a>, despite being a supporter of Ferrari and Michael Schumacher, claimed that it was the "most bloody disgraceful thing I've ever seen in my life" and Schumacher "should have had the balls to move aside and let Barrichello win".<sup id="cite_ref-Nine_Network_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nine_Network-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ferrari were heavily condemned by fans on the internet,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> some members of the Formula One community,<sup id="cite_ref-GuardianRace_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianRace-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TheAgePress_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheAgePress-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> the world's press, and <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Henrique_Cardoso" title="Fernando Henrique Cardoso">Fernando Henrique Cardoso</a> of Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-BetsOff_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BetsOff-65">&#91;N 3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TheAgePress_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheAgePress-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Some Formula One figures held different views, including the Williams pair of Montoya and Ralf Schumacher, and Irvine, who all stated their belief Michael Schumacher should not be apportioned blame for winning the Grand Prix via team orders.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jody_Scheckter" title="Jody Scheckter">Jody Scheckter</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1979_Formula_One_season" title="1979 Formula One season">1979 world champion</a> and Ron Dennis defended Ferrari's application of team orders as a means of enhancing Michael Schumacher's position in the championship.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The day after the race, the FIA summoned Ferrari and its drivers to a meeting of the <a href="/wiki/FIA_World_Motor_Sport_Council" title="FIA World Motor Sport Council">FIA World Motor Sport Council</a> to be held in Paris on 26 June to explain why the team ordered Barrichello to yield the victory to Michael Schumacher and their actions on the podium.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> During a press conference on 24 May, FIA president <a href="/wiki/Max_Mosley" title="Max Mosley">Max Mosley</a> stated Ferrari had not transgressed any regulations on team orders and the meeting would establish the appropriate punishment in the event a panel deemed if any rules were broken, "There are rules about interfering with competition but we established a long time ago that team orders are allowed."<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> That same day, Mosley revealed on behalf of the FIA he wrote a letter of apology to Wolfgang Schüssel.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the meeting, the FIA deemed Ferrari to have transgressed series regulations when Michael Schumacher chose not to mount the first position on the podium and handed the trophy given to him by the Chancellor of Austria to his teammate Barrichello. The council also determined the team had not committed any violation when it invoked team orders on Barrichello to relinquish the victory to Michael Schumacher.<sup id="cite_ref-$1MilliionFineCNN_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-$1MilliionFineCNN-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> It imposed a fine of $1 million on Ferrari, Michael Schumacher and Barrichello, half of which was paid immediately and divided into equal amounts between the trio; the remainder was suspended for one year on the condition a similar offence did not occur.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Neither a points deduction nor a race ban were imposed.<sup id="cite_ref-$1MilliionFineCNN_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-$1MilliionFineCNN-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In response Mosley established a four-member working group to discuss team orders and invited the public to lend their opinion on the practice on the FIA's website.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The FIA accepted feedback from 5 July to 1 September, which was passed on to the working group. They reviewed it and gave their recommendations to the governing body.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> At a meeting of the 26-member Formula One Commission on 28 October, it was confirmed "team orders that interfere with the race result" would be barred from the <a href="/wiki/2003_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="2003 Formula One World Championship">2003 season</a> onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/2010_German_Grand_Prix" title="2010 German Grand Prix">2010 German Grand Prix</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Hockenheimring" title="Hockenheimring">Hockenheimring</a>, Ferrari employed a "coded message"<sup id="cite_ref-:0_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> to invoke team orders to allow driver <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Alonso" title="Fernando Alonso">Fernando Alonso</a> to pass Felipe Massa late on; Alonso went on to win the event. The parallels between how Michael Schumacher and Alonso won those races led the FIA to rescinding the regulation barring team orders in December 2010 because it was deemed difficult to enforce.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Todt admitted to <i><a href="/wiki/La_Stampa" title="La Stampa">La Stampa</a></i> in December 2010 he should have avoided using team orders on Barrichello due to his subsequent belief Michael Schumacher would have won the championship without significant competition.<sup id="cite_ref-LaStampaTodt_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaStampaTodt-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Brawn reiterated his colleague's opinion to British magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Autosport" title="Autosport">Autosport</a></i> seven years later and stated the negative consequences for Formula One outweighed the positives, calling it "on reflection ... it was a mistake."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Race_classification">Race classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2002_Austrian_Grand_Prix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Race classification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-WhitingSatMeeting-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-WhitingSatMeeting_37-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="Fédération Internationale de l&#39;Automobile">Fédération Internationale de l'Automobile</a> race director <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Whiting" title="Charlie Whiting">Charlie Whiting</a> told drivers in a meeting on Saturday afternoon they would be permitted to use the <a href="/wiki/Rumble_strip" title="Rumble strip">rumble strip</a> to the outside of turn one.<sup id="cite_ref-MontoyaPreRace_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MontoyaPreRace-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-TeamOrders-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-TeamOrders_53-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It was the second year in succession that Barrichello had been asked to relinquish a position to his teammate Michael Schumacher on the start/finish straight on the last lap, as he had done so for second position in the <a href="/wiki/2001_Austrian_Grand_Prix" title="2001 Austrian Grand Prix">2001 race</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DawnRace_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DawnRace-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-BetsOff-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-BetsOff_65-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">An Italian online betting company and the Swedish public lottery <a href="/wiki/Svenska_Spel" title="Svenska Spel">Svenska Spel</a> paid out those who bet on Barrichello to win the Grand Prix.<sup id="cite_ref-TheAgePress_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheAgePress-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
